02/08/2025, 3:22 pm - Muzammil New: Mishkat al-Masabih 5954
Ibn `Umar told that 'Umar sent off an army over which he appointed a man called Sariya as commander. While `Umar was addressing the people he began to shout, `Keep near the mountain, Sari[*]" A messenger came later from the army and said, "Commander of the faithful, we met our enemy and they routed us, then someone began to shout, `Keep near the mountain, Sari,' so we set our backs to the mountain and God most high routed them."
*A shortened form of the man's name.

Baihaqi transmitted it in Dala'il an-nubuwa.
وَعَن ابْن عمر أَنَّ عُمَرَ بَعَثَ جَيْشًا وَأَمَّرَ عَلَيْهِمْ رَجُلًا يُدْعَى سَارِيَةَ فَبَيْنَمَا عُمَرُ يَخْطُبُ فَجَعَلَ يَصِيحُ: يَا أَمِيرَ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ لَقِيَنَا عَدُوُّنَا فَهَزَمُونَا فَإِذَا بِصَائِحٍ يَصِيحُ: يَا سَارِيَ الْجَبَلَ. فَأَسْنَدْنَا ظُهُورَنَا إِلَى الْجَبَلِ فَهَزَمَهُمُ اللَّهُ تَعَالَى رَوَاهُ الْبَيْهَقِيُّ فِي دَلَائِل النُّبُوَّة

The most beloved deed to Allah is to make a Muslim happy, or remove one of his troubles, or forgive his debt, or feed his hunger. That I walk with a brother regarding a need is more beloved to me than that I seclude myself in this mosque in Medina for a month. Whoever swallows his anger, then Allah will conceal his faults. Whoever suppresses his rage, even though he could fulfill his anger if he wished, then Allah will secure his heart on the Day of Resurrection. Whoever walks with his brother regarding a need until he secures it for him, then Allah Almighty will make his footing firm across the bridge on the day when the footings are shaken.”

Source: al-Mu’jam al-Awsaṭ lil-Ṭabarānī 6026

03/08/2025, 7:25 am - +971 55 555 3904: السلام عليكم ورحمة الله وبركاته
03/08/2025, 12:25 pm - +966 53 421 5657: The Prophet ﷺ one day visited a villager who honoured him ﷺ as his guest. In return, the Prophet ﷺ invited the villager to his house. When the villager came, the Prophet ﷺ said: “Ask anything that you need.”

The villager was told that he could ask anything that he wished! What did the villager request? He wanted a camel and a goat.

So the Prophet ﷺ used this as a teaching moment to his companions (may Allah be pleased with them all). He ﷺ said: “Were you not able to be like the old lady from Bani Israel?” When the companions asked about her, the Prophet ﷺ explained the following:

When Prophet Musa (peace be upon him) was about to escape from Egypt along with Bani Israel, the scholars of Bani Israel informed him that when death approached Prophet Yusuf (peace be upon him), he took a promise from them that they must take his remains with them if they were ever to leave Egypt. But the only one person from Bani Israel who knew about the location of Prophet Yusuf’s grave was an old lady.

So the old lady was brought to Prophet Musa, and was asked to show the location of Prophet Yusuf’s grave. She agreed, but only with one condition: That Prophet Musa ask from Allah for her one wish.

And what was the request?

To be a neighbour of Prophet Musa in Jannah.

Source: Sahih ibn Hibban

03/08/2025, 1:47 pm - Muzammil New: *Advices from Imam Malik*
______________________________

Mālik ibn Anas (may Allāh have mercy on him) said:
*“Those who would give fatwā from the remnant of knowledge would say: "Allahu a'lam" so perhaps something good would be prepared for him.”* (1)
(the narrator) said: 'And he (Malik) was a man of wisdom and piety (He would say)':
*“Indeed, these people cause confusion for themselves and seek out those who will deceive them.”*
He (also) said: *“The one who is diligent on the boundaries of Islām is not like the one who plays with it.”*
(the narrator) said: 'And he said, who was a man of wisdom and piety':
*“Whatever you play with, do not play with your religion.”*
Then Mālik said:
*“We recite (the Qurʾān), we joke, we rejoice, and we play.”* (2)
[Mā Rawāhu al-Akābir ʿan Mālik (59); Isnād Jayyid]

مَالِكَ بْنَ أَنَسٍ يَقُولُ: "‌‌ كَانَ مَنْ يُفْتِي مِنْ بَقِيَّةِ الْعِلْمِ أَنْ يَقُولَ: لَا أَعْلَمُ؛ فَإِنَّهُ عَسَى أَنْ تُهَيِّأَ لَهُ خَيْرًا قَالَ: وَقَالَ ذَلِكَ الرَّجُلُ، وَكَانَ صَاحِبَ حِكْمَةٍ وَوَرَعٍ: إِنَّ هَؤُلَاءِ يُلْبِسُونَ عَلَى أَنْفُسِهِمْ وَيَلْتَمِسُونَ مَنْ يَغُرُّهُمْ، قَالَ مَالِكُ بْنُ أَنَسٍ: لَيْسَ الْمُتَحَرِّي لِحُدُودِ الْإِسْلَامِ كَالَّذِي يَلْعَبُ فِيهِ، وَقَالَ ذَلِكَ الرَّجُلُ، وَكَانَ صَاحِبَ حِكْمَةٍ وَوَرَعٍ: مَا كُنْتَ لَاعِبًا بِهِ ‌فَلَا ‌تَلْعَبْ ‌بِدِينِكَ، ثُمَّ قَالَ مَالِكٌ: نَقْرَأُ، وَنَمْزَحُ، وَنَفْرَحُ، وَنَلْعَبُ "
[ما رواه الأكابر عن مالك (٥٩) وسنده جيد]

(1) Sahl bin ʿAbdullāh al-Tustarī (D. 283) said:
*"Whoever holds negative assumption is deprived of certainty. And whoever speaks about that which does not concern him is deprived of truthfulness. And whoever busies himself with useless matters is deprived of piety. So if he is deprived of these three, he is destroyed, and he is recorded in the register of the enemies."*
[Ḥilyat al-Awliyāʾ 10/197; Isnād Ḥasan due to Abu Bakr al-Jawrī]

 Anas bin Malik narrated that :
the Messenger of Allah said:   Whoever prays Fajr in congregation, then sits remembering Allah until the sun has risen, then he prays two Rak'ah, then for him is the reward like that of a Hajj and Umrah.   He said:   The Messenger of Allah said: 'Complete, complete, complete.' 

Sunan Tirmizi 586
The Book on Traveling

قال أبو يعلى في المسند (٤٣٦٥):
حَدَّثَنَا شَيْبَانُ بْنُ فَرُّوخَ، حَدَّثَنَا طِيبُ بْنُ سَلْمَانَ، قَالَ: سَمِعْتُ عَمْرَةَ تَقُولُ: سَمِعْتُ أُمَّ الْمُؤْمِنِينَ تَقُولُ: سَمِعْتُ رَسُولَ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَقُولُ: " مَنْ صَلَّى الْفَجْرَ ـ أَوْ قَالَ: الْغَدَاةَ ـ فَقَعَدَ فِي مَقْعَدِهِ فَلَمْ يَلْغُ بِشَيْءٍ مِنْ أَمْرِ الدُّنْيَا، وَيَذْكُرُ اللَّهَ حَتَّى يُصَلِّيَ الضُّحَى أَرْبَعَ رَكَعَاتٍ خَرَجَ مِنْ ذُنُوبِهِ كَيَوْمِ وَلَدَتْهُ أُمُّهُ لَا ذَنْبَ لَهُ "
قلت: سنده حسن
The Messenger of Allah ﷺ  said:
*“Whoever prays Fajr - or he said: the morning prayer - and sits in his place and does not engage in any worldly matter, and remembers Allah until he prays Ḍuḥá four raka'āt, he will emerge from his sins like the day his mother gave birth to him, without any sin.”*

Grading: *Hasan*

04/08/2025, 11:37 pm - Muzammil New: Shaykh Abu Anas Ṭaybī حفظه الله also said it's authentic and gave a full explanation. Summary is as follows 

Innovators consider their innovation as a form of righteousness and therefore aren't usually given the Tawfīq to repent. Especially when the innovation is linked with deep beliefs or exaggerated love for figures like the Prophet (ﷺ) or Ali (رضي الله عنه), making repentance even more difficult. The narration also warns of the severity of bid‘ah by showing Allah's anger and punishment for those who persist.

05/08/2025, 1:31 pm - Muzammil New: Al-Bayhaqī (may Allāh have mercy on him) said:
*“And in the authentic narrations there is sufficiency.”* [Ithbāt ʿAdhāb al-Qabr (234)]
قال البيهقي:
"وفي الآثار ‌الصحيحة ‌غنية" [إثبات عذاب القبر (٢٣٤)]
Al-Sakhāwī (may Allāh have mercy on him) said:
*“And in the authentic (narrations) is sufficiency from the weak ones, as has been established.”* [Istijlāb Irtiqāʾ al-Ghuraf 1/215]
قال السخاوي:
"وفي ‌الصحيح ‌غنية عن الضعيف كما هو مقرر" [استجلاب ارتقاء الغرف ١/ ٢١٥]
Al-Albānī (may Allāh have mercy on him) said:
*“In the authentic (narrations) is that which grants sufficiency from the weak.”* [Tamām al-Minnah, p. 14]
قال الألباني:
"في ‌الصحيح ما ‌يغني عن ‌الضعيف" [تمام المنة ص ١٤]
Al-Wādiʿī (may Allāh have mercy on him) said:
*“So the weak ḥadīth is not needed, and in Allāh's book and the authentic (narrations) from the Sunnah of Allāh's Messenger ﷺ is that which grants sufficiency from the weak.”* [Al-Muqtaraḥ, p. 155]
قال الوادعي:
"فالحديث ‌الضعيف لا يحتاج إليه، وفي كتاب الله وفي ‌الصحيح من سنة رسول الله صلى الله عليه وعلى آله وسلم ما ‌يغني عن ‌الضعيف" [المقترح ص ١٥٥] <This message was edited>

07/08/2025, 12:02 am - +974 5113 3853: Assalamualikum Warahmatullahi Wabarakatuh.

Al-Fudayl b. ʿAyyāḍ [187H] – Allah have mercy on him – said:

“Allah ‘azza wa jalla accepts only those deeds which are both correct and sincere (pure). If the deed is done correctly but not sincerely, it will not be accepted. And if it is sincere but not correct, it will not be accepted.” He was asked, “Abū ‘Alī! What is the sincere and correct deed?” He replied, “The sincere deed is one that is done only for Allah ‘azza wa jall. And the correct deed is one done according to the Sunnah.”

Abū Nu’aym, Hilyah Al-Awliyā` Vol.8 p95..

قال الحافظ الجورقاني في الأباطيل والمناكير والصحاح والمشاهير رقم (122):
أَخْبَرَنَا أَبُو الْفَضْلِ مُحَمَّدُ بْنُ طَاهِرِ بْنِ عَلِيٍّ الْحَافِظُ، أَخْبَرَنَا أَحْمَدُ بْنُ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ أَحْمَدَ، قَالَ: حَدَّثَنَا عِيسَى بْنُ عَلِيِّ بْنِ عَلِيِّ بْنِ عِيسَى، إِمْلَاءً، قَالَ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو الْقَاسِمِ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ بْنُ مُحَمَّدِ بْنِ عَبْدِ الْعَزِيزِ الْبَغَوِيُّ، قَالَ: حَدَّثَنَا أَبُو بَكْرِ بْنُ أَبِي شَيْبَةَ، قَالَ: حَدَّثَنَا عَفَّانُ، عَنْ سَلِيمِ بْنِ حَيَّانَ، عَنْ سَعِيدِ بْنِ مِينَا، عَنْ جَابِرِ بْنِ عَبْدِ اللَّهِ الْأَنْصَارِيِّ وَعَبْدِ اللَّهِ بْنِ عَبَّاسٍ، أَنَّهُمَا قَالَا: «وُلِدَ رَسُولُ اللَّهِ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ يَوْمَ الْفِيلِ، يَوْمَ الِاثْنَيْنِ، الثَّانِي عَشَرَ مِنْ شَهْرِ رَبِيعٍ الْأَوَّلِ، وَفِيهِ بُعِثَ، وَفِيهِ عرجَ إِلَى السَّمَاءِ، وَفِيهِ هَاجَرَ، وَفِيهِ مَاتَ صَلَّى اللَّهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ» <This message was edited>

08/08/2025, 4:02 pm - Muzammil New: Da'if, Ghassaan is majhool
08/08/2025, 4:46 pm - Muzammil New: Definition of a Ṣaḥīḥ ḥadīth
______________________________

ʿAbd al-Raḥmān ibn Mahdī (may Allāh have mercy on him) said:
*Indeed, if a scholar does not know the Sahih from the weak of the ḥadīth, he is not named a scholar. From that which is used to know the authentic ḥadīths from their weak ones is that the ḥadīth must be free of seven characteristics:*
*The first:* that the Shaykh who narrates it is not majrūḥ (criticised).
*The second:* that there is not above him (in the chain) a Majhūl (unknown) Shaykh, by whom the ḥadīth would be nullified.
*The third:* that the ḥadīth is not Mursal (Tabi'i attributing to the Prophet ﷺ), for the mursal, according to us, does not establish a proof.
*The fourth:* that the ḥadīth is not Munqaṭiʿ (disconnected), for the munqaṭiʿ, according to us, is in a worse state than the mursal.
*The fifth:* that the ḥadīth is not muʿḍal (having two consecutive disconnections), for the muʿḍal, according to us, is in a worse state than the munqaṭiʿ.
*The sixth:* that the ḥadīth is not mudallas. For a mudallas ḥadīth has the possibility that (the narrator) has performed tadlīs (skipped his shaykh) and dropped from its isnād the name of a weak narrator, the disclosure of whom would nullify the ḥadīth.
*The seventh:* that the ḥadīth is not muḍṭarib (conflicting), for the muḍṭarib is not used as evidence. (1)

*Therefore, whenever a ḥadīth is found to be free from these characteristics, it is Ṣaḥīḥ. Its acceptance is obligatory, acting upon it is binding, and the one who rejects it is sinful.*

[Al-Jawraqānī (11); Isnād Ḥasan.]

عبد الرحمن بن مهدي، يقول:
*إن العالم إذا لم يعرف الصحيح والسقيم من الحديث لا يسمى عالما فمما يعرف به صحيح الأحاديث من سقيمها أن يكون الحديث متعريا من سبع خصال:*
*فالأول:* أن لا يكون الشيخ الذي يرويه مجروحا.
*والثاني:* أن لا يكون فوقه شيخ مجهول يبطل الحديث به.
*والثالث:* أن لا يكون الحديث مرسلا، فإن المرسل عندنا لا يقوم به الحجة.
*الرابع:* أن لا يكون الحديث منقطعا، فإن المنقطع عندنا أسوأ حالا من المرسل.
*الخامس:* أن لا يكون الحديث معضلا، فإن المعضل عندنا أسوأ حالا من المنقطع.
*السادس:* أن لا يكون الحديث مدَلسا، فإن المدَلس من الأحاديث يحتمل أن يكون قد دلس وأسقط من إسناده اسم راو ضعيف، يبطل الحديث بظهوره.
*السابع:* أن لا يكون الحديث مضطربا، فإن المضطرب لا يحتج به
*فمتى ما وجد الحديث يعرى عن هذه الخصال فهو صحيح قبوله، واجب العمل به لازم، والراد له آثم*

[الجَورقاني (١١) وسنده حسن، التوي وُصف بالفقه ومحدث مكة وهذا بعد تدوين الحديث فهو لا بأس به]

______________________________
(1) The conditions of a Ṣaḥīḥ ḥadīth can be summarised into *"A connected chain of Thiqah (reliable) narrators without any 'illah (defect)"*

09/08/2025, 8:53 am - +92 316 4986376: زادك الله حرصا

Not every language has the capacity to explain or show depth of the words of another.

Sometimes names become -
اصطلاح
A phrase whose meaning cannot be derived merely from understanding the meanings of its individual apparent words.

And معروف
A term which is Famous, well-known, loved by everyone; its opposite is unknown.

Example is people saying خدا in Persian or in Urdu for الله جل جلاله

So if a Muslim who is using English as a medium uses "Verse" to say الآية - Scholars in the fatawa use the term and it's famous and beloved among the Muslims, they know what it means.

Nothing more.
والسلام علیکم ورحمة الله وبركاته <This message was edited>

09/08/2025, 9:12 pm - Muzammil New: *Permissibility of having long mustache provided it doesn't touch lips* (1)
______________________________

*Isḥāq ibn ʿĪsā al-Ṭabbāʿ said: I saw Mālik ibn Anas and he had an abundant moustache with two long ends. So I asked him about that and he said: "Zayd ibn Aslam narrated to me from ʿĀmir ibn ʿAbdullāh ibn al-Zubayr from his father that when a matter distressed ʿUmar ibn al-Khaṭṭāb, he would twist his moustache and blow." So he (Mālik) gave me the ruling by citing the ḥadīth.*
[Al-ʿIlal by Aḥmad (1589); Isnād Ṣaḥīḥ]

And in another narration:
*When ʿUmar became angry, he would twist his moustache.*
[Al-Āḥād wa al-Mathānī (78) and Maʿrifat al-Ṣaḥābah by Abū Nuʿaym (171); Isnād Ṣaḥīḥ]

And in another narration:
*A man from the people of the desert came to ʿUmar ibn al-Khaṭṭāb and said: "O leader of the believers, our lands! we fought for them in the Jāhiliyyah (pre-Islamic era) and accepted Islām upon them, and now they are declared protected pasture (ḥimā) against us?" So ʿUmar began to blow and twist his moustache.*
[Ibn Saʿd (3/303); Isnād Ṣaḥīḥ]

*إسحاق بن عيسى الطباع قال رأيت مالك بن أنس وافر الشارب لشاربه ذنبتان فسأتله عن ذلك فقال حدثني زيد بن أسلم عن عامر بن عبد الله بن الزبير عن أبيه أن عمر بن الخطاب كان إذا كربه أمر ‌فتل ‌شاربه ونفخ فأفتاني بالحديث*
[العلل لأحمد (١٥٨٩) وسنده صحيح]
وفي رواية:
*كان عمر إِذا غضب فتل شاربه* 
[الآحاد والمثاني (٧٨) ومعرفة الصحابة لأبي نعيم (١٧١) وسنده صحيح]
وفي رواية:
*أن عمر بن الخطاب أتاه رجل من أهل البادية فقال: يا أمير المؤمنين بلادنا قاتلنا عليها في الجاهلية وأسلمنا عليها في الإسلام ثم تحمى علينا؟ فجعل عمر ينفخ ويفتل شاربه*
[ابن سعد (٣/٣٠٣) وسنده صحيح]

al-Mughīrah ibn Shuʿbah (may Allah be pleased with him) said:
*My moustache had become overgrown, so Allāh's Messenger ﷺ trimmed it for me on a siwāk.*
[Aḥmad (18212), Abū Dāwūd (188), al-Shamāʾil (167), al-Āḥād wa al-Mathānī (1550), al-Muʿjam al-Kabīr (1059, 1061), and al-Tamhīd (13/206); with Jayyid asānīd]

عن المغيرة بن شعبة، رضي الله عنه قال: كان شاربي قد وفى، ‌فقصه رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم على ‌سواك
[أحمد (١٨٢١٢)، وأبو داود (١٨٨)، والشمائل (١٦٧)، والآحاد والمثاني (١٥٥٠)، والمعجم الكبير (١٠٥٩، ١٠٦١)، والتمهيد (١٣/٢٠٦) بأسانيد جياد]

10/08/2025, 4:06 am - +92 316 4986376: *Benefit*: (In Manāqib al-Shāfiʿī, 1/166) Al-Bayhaqī (رحمه الله) explained the reason Imām Aḥmad (رحمه الله) said regarding Imām al-Shāfiʿī (رحمه الله):

“His (narration of) ḥadīth is authentic, and his opinion is correct.”

What he meant was that Imām al-Shāfiʿī would rely solely upon well-known, authentic aḥādīth, and he would reject anything not firmly established unlike some scholars who, at times, gave preference to analogy (qiyās) or personal preference (istiḥsān) over authentic narrations, or relied upon weak or mursal reports and narrations from unknown narrators.

I (Abū Bakr ibn Yāsir al-Shāfiʿī) say: In the words of Imām al-Bayhaqī is evidence for a qāʿidah in Uṣūl al-Fiqh according to Ahl al-Ḥadīth that *sound analogy (qiyās ṣaḥīḥ) is to be given precedence over any weak or mursal narration.*

*"Every religion has knights and the knights of this religion are the people of Asānīd (chains of narration)."* (1)
[Sharaf Aṣḥāb al-Ḥadīth (p. 44); Isnād Jayyid]

يَزِيدَ بْنِ زُرَيْعٍ، يَقُولُ: "لِكُلِّ دِينٍ فُرْسَانٌ وَفُرْسَانُ هَذَا الدِّينِ أَصْحَابُ الْأَسَانِيدِ"
[شرف أصحاب الحديث (ص ٤٤) وسنده جيد]
______________________________
(1) The true weapon of the believer is not the spear nor the shield, but rather that connected chain of narration which is filled with the names of the trustworthy narrators. It is the fortress of knowledge and religion. Through it, a statement is established, the authentic is known from the weak, the transmission of the legislation is made sound, and doubts are lifted. This is why al-Imām al-Shāfiʿī said about Ahl al-Ḥadīth: *“Upon you is the Companions of Ḥadīth for indeed they are the most correct people.”* [Dhamm al-Kalām li al-Harawī (395); isnād Ḥasan]

[Abū Bakr al-Lāhūrī al-Shāfiʿī]

عَنِ ابْنِ مَسْعُودٍ رَضِيَ اللهُ عَنهُ عَنِ النَّبيِّ صَلَّى اللهُ عَلَيْهِ وَسَلَّمَ أَنَّهُ قَال: سُورَةُ تَبَارَكَ هِيَ المَانِعَةُ مِن عَذَابِ القَبر.

14/08/2025, 12:30 am - Taha Kamran: IMG-20250814-WA0047.jpg (file attached)
14/08/2025, 12:30 am - Syed Abdullah: 
14/08/2025, 12:31 am - Taha Kamran: You deleted this message
14/08/2025, 1:37 am - +92 316 4986376: السلام علیکم ورحمة الله وبركاته 

This is not in the book as far as I have read the book.

Another reason I think this is not correct is because it seems to be romanticized likely to promote the modern idea of love.

The Author (Ibn al Jawzi) literally named a chapter
لذت الدنيا شيبت بالنغص
*Worldly pleasures are mingled with distress/misery.*

Whoever reflects upon the world will realize that it contains no pure pleasure at all. And if any pleasure is found, it is mixed with troubles that far outweigh the pleasure many times over.

He goes on to say....*Among such pleasures* _(which bring misery/distress)_ *are women*: perhaps the one thought beautiful does not remain so, or perhaps she does not love her husband. Once that is known (that she does not love her) he should keep away from her. Perhaps she betrays and that is destruction. And even if all desires are fulfilled (with the woman), the thought of separation (from her) adds more pain than the pleasure itself.

Page no. 489, Publication by Dar ul Qalam - Damishq (see on https://shamela.ws/book/12028/803)

------------

Nevertheless, Quran talks about it in clear terms:
وَمِنْ آيَاتِهِ أَنْ خَلَقَ لَكُمْ مِنْ أَنفُسِكُمْ أَزْوَاجًا لِّتَسْكُنُوا إِلَيْهَا … (الروم:21)
“One of His signs is that He created for you mates so that you may find tranquility in them…”

______________________________

Abū Saʿīd al-Khudrī (may Allāh be pleased with him) said:
*“The Prophet ﷺ sat one day upon the Minbar, and we sat around him.”* [Al-Bukhārī (921) and Muslim (1052)]

أبو سعيد الخدري قال: إن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم جلس ذات ‌يوم ‌على ‌المنبر ‌وجلسنا ‌حوله [البخاري (٩٢١) ومسلم (١٠٥٢)]
Al-Mustamirr bin al-Rayyān said:
*“I saw Anas (bin Mālik) at the first gate on Friday having faced the Minbar (pulpit).”* (1)
[Muṣannaf Ibn Abī Shaybah (5339); Isnād Ṣaḥīḥ]

In another narration he said:
*“I saw Anas bin Mālik come on Friday and he leaned against the wall and faced the Imām.”*
[Al-Awsat by Ibn al-Mundhir (1802); Isnād Ṣaḥīḥ]

‌المستمر بن الريان قال: رأيت ‌أنسا عند الباب الأول يوم الجمعة قد ‌استقبل المنبر
[مصنف ابن أبي شيبة (٥٣٣٩) وسنده صحيح]

المستمر بن الريان، قال: رأيت ‌أنس بن مالك جاء يوم الجمعة فاستند إلى الحائط، ‌واستقبل الإِمام
[الأوسط لابن المنذر (١٨٠٢) وسنده صحيح]

______________________________
(1) Ibn ʿAbd al-Barr (D. 463) said:
*“(It is) a recommended Sunnah according to the scholars; I do not know of them disagreeing in that.”* [Al-Istidhkār (2/50)]

18/08/2025, 12:30 pm - Muzammil New: *You will be questioned for what you attribute.* Allah said _*On the Day their tongues, their hands, and their feet will witness against them for what they used to do.*_ [24:24]
______________________________

*ʿAlī bin al-Ḥasan said: I heard ʿAbdullāh bin al-Mubārak say: “If you are tested with judgement, then upon you is the Athar (narration).”  So I mentioned this to Abū Ḥamzah Muḥammad bin Maymūn al-Sukkarī, from the people of Marw, there is no harm in his (narration), and he said: “Do you know what the Athar is? It is that I narrate something to you, and you act upon it. Then, on the Day of Resurrection, you are asked, Who commanded you to do this? and you say, Abū Ḥamzah. Then I am brought forth, and it is said, This person claims that you commanded him to do such-and-such. If I say, ‘Yes,’ you are released and I am asked ‘From where did you say this?’ I will say, Al-Aʿmash told me. Then al-Aʿmash is questioned, and if he says ‘Yes’, I am released and al-Aʿmash is asked, ‘From where did you say this?’ He will say, Ibrāhīm told me. Then Ibrāhīm is questioned, and if he says, ‘Yes,’ al-Aʿmash is released, and Ibrāhīm is taken and asked, ‘From where did you say this?’ He will say, ʿAlqamah told me. Then ʿAlqamah is questioned, and if he says, ‘Yes,’ Ibrāhīm is released, and he (ʿAlqamah) is asked, ‘From where did you say this?’ He will say, ʿAbdullāh bin Masʿūd told me. Then ʿAbdullāh is questioned, and if he says ‘Yes’, ʿAlqamah is released, and Bin Masʿūd is asked, ‘From where did you say this?’ He will say, ‘The Messenger of Allāh ﷺ told me.’ Then the Messenger of Allāh ﷺ is questioned, and if he says, ‘Yes,’ Bin Masʿūd is released. Then the Prophet ﷺ is asked, and he will say, ‘Jibrīl told me,’ until it reaches the Lord, the Blessed and Exalted. So this is the Athar. The matter is serious, not a jest, as it borders upon Paradise or Hellfire, between which there is no other abode. And let each one of you know that he is responsible for his religion and for how he took its lawful and unlawful matters; like that which Ashhal bin Ḥātim narrated to me from Bin ʿAwn from Muḥammad (bin Sīrīn), who said: ‘Indeed, this knowledge is religion, so let a man consider from whom he takes his religion.’*

[Aḥwāl al-Rijāl (358-359); Isnād Ṣaḥīḥ]

علي بن الحسن قال سمعت عبد الله يعني ابن المبارك يقول إذا ابتليت بالقضاء فعليك بالأثر قال علي فذكرته لأبي حمزة محمد بن ميمون السكري من أهل مرو لا بأس به فقال هل تدري ما الأثر أن أحدثك بالشيء فتعمل به فيقال لك يوم القيامة من أمرك بهذا فتقول أبو حمزة فيجاء بي فيقال إن هذا يزعم أنك أمرته بكذا وكذا فإن قلت نعم خلي عنك ويقال لي من أين قلت هذا فأقول قال لي الأعمش فيسأل الأعمش فإذا قال نعم خلي عني ويقال للأعمش من أين قلت فيقول قال لي إبراهيم فيسأل إبراهيم فإن قال نعم خلي عن الأعمش وأخذ إبراهيم فيقال له من أين قلت فيقول قال لي علقمة فيسأل علقمة فإذا قال نعم خلي عن إبراهيم ويقال له من أين قلت فيقول قال لي عبد الله بن مسعود فيسال عبد الله فان قال نعم خلي عن علقمة ويقال لابن مسعود من أين قلت قال فيقول قال لي رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فيسأل رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم فإن قال نعم خلي عن ابن مسعود فيقال للنبي صلى الله عليه وسلم فيقول قال لي جبريل حتى ينتهي إلى الرب تبارك وتعالى فهذا الأثر فالأمر جد غير هزل إذ كان يشفي على جنة أو نار ليس بينهما هناك منزل وليعلم أحدكم أنه مسؤول عن دينه وعن أخذه حله وحرامه كالذي حدثني أشهل بن حاتم عن ابن عون عن محمد قال إن هذا العلم دين فلينظر امرؤ عمن يأخذ دينه

[أحوال الرجال (ص ٣٥٨-٣٥٩) وسنده صحيح]

Imam Ibn al-Jawzi (rahimahullah) said:

"My brothers, travel is decreed for us. So why do we seek to reside in an abode that is not ours to dwell in permanently? The years are stations, the months are stops, the days are miles, the breaths are steps, sins are obstacles, profit is Paradise, and loss is Hellfire."

[Bahru ad-Dumu, Chapter 9]

Authenticity please, may Allaah be pleased with all of us'

20/08/2025, 8:41 pm - +92 316 4986376: السلام عليكم ورحمة الله وبركاته

The wording 
"غفرانك"
It is proven from the Prophet ﷺ through the narration of Umm ul Mu'mineen Ayesha (may Allah be pleased with her) – Alhamdulillah.
[ Tirmidhi:7 – Darimi:707 – Al Adab Al Mufrad:693 – Musnad Ahmad:25520 and others ]

As for the last part 
"الحمد لله الذي اذهب عني الاذى وعافاني"
then its chain is weak to the Prophet ﷺ due to Ismail bin Muslim al Makki (who is Munkar al Hadith) in the narration. Many scholars graded it weak – from them Al Albani and Zubair Ali Zai (may Allah have mercy on them).
[ Sunan Ibn Majah:301 – Nasai Kubra:9825 – Ibn Sinni:22 and others ] <This message was edited>
20/08/2025, 8:53 pm - +92 316 4986376: وبه قال البلوشي
20/08/2025, 9:02 pm - +92 316 4986376: وعليكم السلام ورحمة الله وبركاته

قال الإمام ابن جوزي رحمه الله:
إخواني، السفر مكتوب علينا، فما لنا نطلب الإقامة في جار ليست لنا دار مقامة؟ السنون منازل، والشهور مراحل، والأيام أميال، والأنفاس خطوات، والمعاصي قطاع، والربح الجنة، والخسران النار.

My brothers, travel is decreed for us. So why do we seek to reside in an abode that is not ours to dwell in permanently? The years are stations, the months are stops, the days are miles, the breaths are steps, sins are obstacles, profit is Paradise, and loss is Hellfire.

24/08/2025, 8:39 pm - Muzammil New: *Whoever desires honour then to Allah belongs all honour* [35:10]
_______________________________

Ṭāriq bin Shihāb said:
*’Umar bin al-Khaṭṭāb set out for Shām while Abu 'Ubaydah ibn al-Jarrāḥ was with us. They came upon a shallow ford and 'Umar was on his camel. He dismounted from it, took off his Khuffayn (leather socks), placed them on his shoulder, and took the reins of his camel then waded with it through the ford. Abu 'Ubaydah said, O Amir al-Muminin, are you doing this? You take off your Khuffain and place them on your shoulder, and take the reins of your camel, and crossed with it through the ford? It would not please me if the people of the country were to see you in this state. ‘Umar said: Awih! (an expression of disappointment). If anyone other than you, O Abu 'Ubaydah, had said this, I would have made him (by punishment) an example for the Ummah of Muhammad  ﷺ. Indeed we were the most humiliated people and Allah gave us honour through Islam. So whenever we seek honour through other than what Allah has honoured us with, Allah will humiliate us.*

[al-Mustadrak 207,4529; Ṣaḥīḥ asānīd]

خرج عمر بن الخطاب إلى الشام، ومعنا أبو عبيدة بن الجراح، فأتوا على مخاضة، وعمر على ناقة له، فنزل عنها، وخلع خفيه، فوضعهما على عاتقه، وأخذ بزمام ناقته، فخاض بها المخاضة، فقال أبو عبيدة: يا أمير المؤمنين، أأنت تفعل هذا، أتخلع خفيك وتضعهما على عاتقك، وتأخذ بزمام ناقتك، ‌وتخوض ‌بها ‌المخاضة؟ ما يسرني أن أهل البلد استشرفوك. فقال عمر: أوه، لو يقل ذا غيرك أبا عبيدة، جعلته نكالا لأمة محمد ﷺ، إنا كنا أذل قوم فأعزنا الله بالإسلام، فمهما نطلب العزة بغير ما أعزنا الله به أذلنا الله

25/08/2025, 6:07 am - Mohamed Ahmed Abdulwahab: *I don't think it's authentic because the wording Ibn Qayyim said that it's the right of the father and not the mother.*

His words:

الْخَامِس فِي أَن التَّسْمِيَة حق للْأَب *لَا للْأُم*

هَذَا مِمَّا لَا نزاع فِيهِ بَين النَّاس وَأَن الْأَبَوَيْنِ إِذا تنَازعا فِي تَسْمِيَة الْوَلَد فَهِيَ للْأَب

On the fact that naming is the right of the father, *not the mother*

This is something about which there is no disagreement among the people. And if the father and mother dispute over naming the child, then the right belongs to the father.

Memorizing the Qur'an After the Age of Fifty (50)

Shaykh 'Abd al-Mushin al-'Abbad - may Allah preserve and protect him - was asked in his home: Is an individual able to memorize the Qur'an after reaching the age of fifty?

He replied: Yes, and I am from those who memorized the Qur'an after the age of fifty! There were Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) who Islam reached them when they were older; despite that they memorized.

16th of Jumada al-Akhirah 1441H

*Isnad Hasan* 

Imam Ḥākim added (and similar is said by al-Quḍāʿī ash-Shāfiʿī):
بالتشديد من الحب، وأما بالتخفيف من المحاباة
"With tashdīd (doubling), it comes from love; but with takhfīf (lightening), it comes from showing favoritism."

أخرجه البخاري في الأدب المفرد (رقم ٥٩٤)، والبيهقي في شعب الإيمان (٦/٨٩٧٦) والسنن الكبرى (١١٧٢٦) والآداب (رقم ٨١)، وأبو الشيخ في الأمثال (رقم ٢٤٥)، وتمام الرازي في الفوائد (٢/١٥٧٧)، وابن عدي في الكامل (٤/١٠٤)، وابن عساكر في تاريخ دمشق (٦١/٢٢٥، ٢٢٧)، وابن عبد البر في التمهيد (٢١/١٧–١٨) والاستذكار (٨/٢٩٢–٢٩٣)، والحاكم في معرفة علوم الحديث (ص٨٠)، والدولابي في الكنى (٢/٤٦٦، ٦٤٨)، والمزي في تهذيب الكمال (١٣/٣١٣) والقضاعي في مسند الشهاب (١/٣٨١) وقال العراقي إسناده جيد والحافظ ابن حجر في تلخيص الحبير (٣/ ٧٠) قال: إسناده حسن. وكذا حسنه الألباني في الإرواء (١٦٠١)، وصحيح الجامع (٣٠٠٤) *وبه قال البلوشي.*

The weak among you are strong in my sight so I will relieve their suffering as is their right, if Allah wills. The strong among you are weak in my sight so I will take what is due from them, if Allah wills. No people abandon jihad in the way of Allah but that Allah strikes them with disgrace. Indeed, I heard him in his early days (in his youth) say: “Sometimes my mind pauses at a matter, or an issue, or a situation that becomes difficult for me. Then I seek forgiveness from Allah Most High a thousand times, or more, or less, until my chest is expanded and the difficulty is resolved.”

He said: “And at that time I might be in the market, or the mosque, or the street, or the school (madrassah) yet none of that would prevent me from remembrance and seeking forgiveness until I attain what I seek.”

The Author says:
This matter is about holding fast to what the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and his Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) were upon, and avoiding what the Prophet ﷺ warned against when he said: “Beware of newly invented matters, for every innovation is a bidʿah, and every bidʿah is misguidance.” He also said: “The worst of matters are those newly introduced; every newly introduced matter is a bidʿah, every bidʿah is misguidance, and every misguidance leads to the Fire.”

Based on this, those who take the Mawlid (the Prophet’s birthday) as an ‘Eid are not among those who are expected to be rewarded for such an innovation. Rather, they are among those who are feared to face punishment for opposing what the Messenger of Allah ﷺ and his Companions (may Allah be pleased with them) were upon.

Furthermore, Allah the Most High said:
{And whatever the Messenger gives you, take it; and whatever he forbids you from, then abstain. And fear Allah; indeed, Allah is severe in punishment.} [Al-Hashr: 7]

In this verse is a severe warning for whoever opposes the command of the Messenger ﷺ and commits what he forbade. Included in this is the practice of taking the Mawlid as an Eid.

Not the exact wording
https://sunnah.com/bukhari:6072

Ibn Hajar رحمه الله said in it's Sharh in Fath' ul Bari (Vol. 10, Pg. 504):

The meaning of “taking by the hand” is what it implies: gentleness and willing obedience/help. It includes different forms of showing humility, such as preferring a woman over a man, or a slave over a free person. 

The text generalizes by using the word “female slave” (basically any servant woman), and “wherever she wished” refers to any place.

The wording “taking by the hand” indicates the utmost care and attention, even if her need was outside the city, and he sought to help her in that matter. This shows his extreme humility and complete freedom from all forms of pride عليه الصلاة والسلام 

There's another wording under the Chapter: Freedom from arrogance, and having humility
https://sunnah.com/ibnmajah:4177

27/08/2025, 3:31 am - +92 316 4986376: وعليكم السلام ورحمة الله وبركاته

We as people sometimes give precedence to the sayings of the scholars over the evidences they use. SubhanAllah.

---------------
Ibn al Qayyim رحمه الله mentioned the *(Ayah 5: Surah al-Ahzaab)* and said:

A child follows his mother in freedom or slavery, but follows his father in lineage and his name (i.e. right of his name), *because lineage and attribution go back to the father*........Naming, teaching, and `aqīqah are the responsibility of the father, not the mother. 

The Prophet ﷺ said: “A child was born to me last night, so *I named him* after my father Ibrāhīm” (Muslim, 2315).....
(Tuhfat al-Mawdūd, 1/197, Ibn al-Qayyim, d. 751 AH).

Ibn Taymiyyah رحمه الله mentioned the same in Majmū‘ al-Fatāwā (29/326).

------------------
Shayjh As-Sa‘dī رحمه الله commenting on the Ayah : “And the male is not like the female, and I have named her Maryam” *(Surah Āl ʿImrān: Ayah 36)*, said: This indicates preference of male over female, permissibility of naming at birth, and that the *mother may name the child if the father does not object.*

---------------------

In Nihāyat al-Muhtāj (Vol. 9 and Pg no. 372) by Ibn Hajar al-Haytami ash-Shafiee عفا الله عنه, it is mentioned: *Naming is the right of the guardian,* which is the father even if he is poor and cannot provide maintenance and then the grandfather if the father is absent. 

(And majority from other schools of thought say the same)

---------------------

The wife’s rights are protected in all affairs, as Allah says: “And for them (wives) are *rights similar to those upon them,* in a fair manner” (Al-Baqarah : Ayah 228).

And Allah says: “And their affairs are [conducted] by *mutual consultation*” (Ash-Shūrā : Ayah 38). 

So I say: The correct view is that naming should ideally be through mutual consultation between husband and wife. And if the wife names the child and father does not object then there's no problem with that. But if there is a dispute or disagreement, then the father has priority, as it seems from the evidences. والله أعلم <This message was edited>

A brother is asking

I have a question regarding the story of the two men who came to the Messenger of Allah ﷺ while they had shaved their beards and left their mustaches long. The Messenger ﷺ disapproved of them and asked: “Who commanded you with this?” They replied: “Our Lord commanded us to do so.” So the Messenger ﷺ said: “Rather, my Lord has commanded me to let my beard grow and to trim my mustache.”

What is the authenticity of this narration?

27/08/2025, 6:15 pm - +92 316 4986376: وعليكم السلام ورحمة الله وبركاته

The Author said in Madarik al-Naẓar fī al-Siyāsah (vol. 1, pp. 339–342, جامع الكتب الإسلامية edition):

It has been attributed to the Shaykh (Ibn Uthaymeen) that he allows protests, sit-ins, and other such practices that come from the disbelieving West. So it is necessary to quote his actual words (May Allah have mercy on him) as he was asked about it in Muharram of the year 1416 AH and he replied:

As for me, people lie about me a lot! I ask Allah to guide those who lie about me and stop them from doing so again.......

The Prophet ﷺ commanded that if someone sees from his leader something he dislikes, he should be patient. He said: ‘Whoever dies without an Imam dies a death of ignorance.’

Our duty is to give advice as much as possible, but openly challenging rulers and holding protests is against the way of the Salaf. Now you can see clearly that these actions have nothing to do with the Shari‘ah, nor with real reform. They only bring harm.

Therefore, we do not support demonstrations, sit-ins, or similar things at all. We absolutely do not support them. Reform can be achieved without them. But it seems there are hidden hands; whether inside or outside that are pushing such ideas.

The newspaper Al-Muslimoon, issue no. 540, page 10 — Friday, 11th of Muharram, 1416 AH.
جريدة المسلمون، عدد (540) ص (10) ـ الجمعة (11 المحرم 1416هـ)
https://ketabonline.com/ar/books/25790/read?page=342&part=1#p-25790-342-1

As for the Newspaper it's not available online and I couldn't find it.


And Ibn ʿUthaymīn’s position is clear in his fatawa if we summarize his position:

In Muslim countries, protests are completely forbidden and not allowed at all. In non-Muslim countries, they may be allowed only in cases of real necessity if there is no other way to secure the rights of muslims. Beware they usually lead to chaos, theft, mixing of men and women, and open the door to many evils. The harm is greater than the benefit, even if sometimes there seems to be a short-term benefit.

https://alathar.net/home/esound/index.php?op=codevi&coid=65655

I have this in my notes. The authentic version doesn't mention *what* is Ruwaybidah. The following version has been authenticated by al-Albani, Zubair 'Ali Zai and Shu'ayb al-Arnaut 

عَنْ أَبِي هُرَيْرَةَ، قَالَ: قَالَ رَسُولُ اللهِ صلى الله عليه وسلم: " قَبْلَ السَّاعَةِ سِنُونَ خَدَّاعَةٌ، يُكَذَّبُ فِيهَا الصَّادِقُ، وَيُصَدَّقُ فِيهَا الْكَاذِبُ، وَيُخَوَّنُ فِيهَا الْأَمِينُ، وَيُؤْتَمَنُ فِيهَا الْخَائِنُ، وَيَنْطِقُ فِيهَا الرُّوَيْبِضَةُ ". قَالَ سُرَيْجٌ في روايته: وَيَنْظُرُ فِيهَا لِلرُّوَيْبِضَةِ [مسند أحمد (٨٤٥٩): إسناد حسن]
قَالَ ابْنُ الْأَثِيرِ: "الْعَاجِزُ الَّذِي رَبَضَ عَنْ مَعَالِي الْأُمُورِ وَقَعَدَ عَنْ طَلَبِهَا" [النهاية ٢/١٨٥]

28/08/2025, 7:12 pm - +92 316 4986376: *Virtue of sharing knowledge*
______________________________

Abū al-Dardāʾ, may Allāh the most High be pleased with him said:
*“Learn before knowledge is lifted. Indeed, the lifting of knowledge is the departure of scholars. Indeed, the scholar and the student are equal in reward. (1) And the only (successful) people are two: a scholar and a student. And there is no good other than that. (2)”*

[Ḥilyat al-Awliyāʾ (1/213) & al-Zuhd by Aḥmad (727); Both isnād Ḥasan]

عن أبي الدرداء رضي الله تعالى عنه. قال: تعلموا قبل أن يرفع العلم، إن رفع العلم ذهاب العلماء، إن العالم والمتعلم في الأجر سواء، وإنما الناس رجلان، عالم ومتعلم، ولا خير فيما بين ذلك.
[حلية الأولياء (١/٢١٣) والزهد لأحمد (٧٢٧) وسندهما حسن]

(1) The equality here is in sharing the stream of reward - the scholar by teaching the deen, and the student by preserving and transmitting; while the ignorant remains cut off from that chain.

(2) The negation “no good” means all other pursuits - wealth, status, deeds without knowledge - are nothing against the worth of knowledge and it is the measure that makes people valued. Ibn al-Qayyim said, *“Allah made knowledge to hearts as rain to the earth…there is no life of the heart except by knowledge”* (Miftāḥ Dār al-Saʿādah 478/1)

[Abū Bakr bin Yāsir al-Shāfi'ī]

Abu Huraira reported: 
The Messenger of Allah, peace and blessings be upon him, said, “Woe to the Arabs for an evil tribulation approaching like darkest part of the night! A man will wake up as believer but by evening will become an unbeliever. People will sell their religion for some pitiful gains in the world. The one who adheres to his religion on that day will be as if he were grasping a hot coal or a bundle of thorns.”

Source: Musnad Aḥmad 9073

" *Go forth as a scholar or as a Student of Knowledge, and do not set out as al-imma'ah between the two.* "

عَنْ زِرٍّ قَالَ: قَالَ عَبْدُ اللَّهِ (ابن مسعود - رضي الله عنه): « *اغْدُ عَالِمًا أَوْ مُتَعَلِّمًا وَلَا تَغْدُ إِمَّعَةً بَيْنَ ذَلِكَ* »

30/08/2025, 9:39 am - +60 19-310 1311: A story on the virtues of seeking ilm
Imam Ibn Batal said in Sharh Sahih al-Bukhari 1/133-135:
The virtue of knowledge has many effects, and one of the best of them is what Yunus ibn Abdullah narrated to me, saying:
Abu Isa Yahya ibn Abdullah told us, saying: Saeed ibn Fahlun told us, saying: Abu al-Ala’ Abdul A’la ibn Ma’la told us, saying: Usman ibn Ayub told us, saying: Yahya ibn Yahya narrated to me, saying:
The first thing Malik ibn Anas told me when I came to him seeking knowledge, inspired by what Allah had guided me to on the first day I sat with him, he asked me: “What is your name?” I said: “May Allah honor you, Yahya,” and I was young among my companions. He said to me: “O Yahya, be earnest in this matter, and I will tell you a narration that will encourage you in it and deter you from other matters.”
He said: “A young boy from the people of Sham came to Medina at an age like yours. He was diligent and sought knowledge with us until death came to him. I saw at his funeral something I had never seen for anyone from our town, neither student nor scholar.”
I saw all the scholars crowding around his bier. When the ruler saw this, he refrained from leading the prayer over him and said: “Bring forward whoever you wish from among you.” So the scholars brought forward Rabi’ah, then carried him to his grave.
Malik said: “Rabi’ah, Zaid ibn Aslam, Yahya ibn Sa’eed, Ibn Shihab, and those closest to them—Muhammad ibn al-Mundhir, Safwan ibn Sulaym, Abu Hazim, and others like them—placed the funeral clay on Rabi’ah’s grave, and all of them handled the clay.”
Malik said: “On the third day after his burial, a man from the best people of our town saw him in the finest form—a young boy, fair-skinned, wearing a green turban, with a chestnut horse descending from the sky beneath him, as if it were coming to him deliberately and greeting him.”
And he said: “Knowledge has reached him.” The man asked him: “And what has reached you?”
He said: “Allah gave me a rank in Paradise for every branch of knowledge I learned, but the ranks did not reach the level of the scholars. Then Allah said: ‘Increase the heirs of My Prophets.’ He guaranteed to Himself that whoever dies as a scholar of My Sunnah, or a follower of My Prophets’ Sunnah, or a seeker of that knowledge, I will gather them in one rank. So my Lord gave me until I reached the level of the scholars. There are only two ranks between me and the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him): a rank in which he sits surrounded by all the Prophets, and a rank with all his companions, and all the companions of the Prophets who followed them, and the rank after them includes all the scholars and seekers. He guided me until I stood among them, and they said to me: ‘Welcome, welcome, except for what more Allah has in store for me.’”
The man asked him: “And what about Malik with Allah, is there more?” He said: “He promised me that all the Prophets will be gathered as you saw them in one group. He will say: ‘O scholars, this is My Paradise that I have made lawful for you, and this is My pleasure that I am pleased with you. You shall not enter Paradise until you desire and intercede, and I will give you whatever you wish and allow you to intercede for those for whom you intercede, so that My servants see your honor with Me and your status with Me.’”
When the man awoke, he narrated it to the scholars, and its news spread throughout Medina.
Malik said: “There were people in Medina who began seeking this matter with us but then abandoned it until they heard this narration. They returned to it with determination, and today they are among the scholars of our town. O Yahya, be earnest in this matter.”
The author said: “However, the virtue of knowledge is only for those who act upon it and intend in seeking it the pleasure of Allah, the Exalted.”
30/08/2025, 11:53 am - Muzammil New: @⁨Mohamed Ahmed Abdulwahab⁩
30/08/2025, 11:54 am - Muzammil New: *Sunnah of Kaffarat al-Majlis (Expiation of gathering) after reciting Qur'an and finishing obligatory prayers*
______________________________

ʿĀʾishah (may Allāh be pleased with her) said:
Allāh's Messenger ﷺ never sat in a gathering, nor recited Qurʾān *(1)*, nor prayed a prayer, except that he concluded that with (certain) words. So I said: *O Messenger of Allāh, I see that you do not sit in a gathering, nor recite the Qurʾān, nor pray a prayer, except that you conclude with these words?* He said: *“Yes. Whoever has said good, a seal will be placed for him upon that good, and for whoever has said evil, they will be an expiation for him:* *Subḥānaka wa biḥamdika, lā ilāha illā Anta, astaghfiruka wa atūbu ilayk’* (Perfection and praise belong to You (O Allāh). There is none deserving worship but You. I seek Your forgiveness and repent to You).

[Al-Nasāʾī in al-Kubrā (10067) and ʿAmal al-Yawm wa al-Laylah (307); Isnād Ṣaḥīḥ]

عن ‌عائشة قالت: ما جلس رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم مجلسا قط، ولا تلا ‌قرآنا، ولا صلى ‌صلاة إلا ختم ذلك بكلمات قالت: فقلت: يا رسول الله، أراك ما تجلس مجلسا، ولا تتلو ‌قرآنا، ولا تصلي ‌صلاة إلا ختمت بهؤلاء الكلمات؟ قال: نعم، من قال خيرا ختم له طابع على ذلك الخير، ومن قال شرا كن له كفارة: ‌سبحانك وبحمدك، لا إله إلا أنت، أستغفرك وأتوب إليك
[النسائي في الكبرى (١٠٠٦٧) وعمل اليوم والليلة (٣٠٧) وسنده صحيح]

عن ابن مسعود رضي الله عنه:
لا تُقَلِّدوا دينَكُمُ الرِّجالَ، فإِن أبَيتُم فبِالأمواتِ لا بالأحياءِ 

*Do not do taqlid (i.e., blind follow) men in your religion. But if you must deny me (i.e., oppose what I say), then follow the dead, not the living.*

2) Mention how you want the answer (i.e summarised, takhrīj, scan, voice message etc) to avoid back and forth

01/09/2025, 6:34 pm - Mohamed Ahmed Abdulwahab: *Difference between a hypocrite and a believer*
______________________________

Al-Ḥasan (al-Baṣrī) said:
*“Indeed, the people are among three types: a believer, a hypocrite, and a disbeliever. As for the believer, he acts in obedience to Allāh, the Mighty and Majestic. As for the disbeliever, Allāh, the most High, has certainly humiliated him as you have seen. And as for the hypocrite, he is here and there; In the private chambers, the houses, and the paths. We seek refuge in Allāh. By Allāh, they did not know their Rabb; rather, their denial of their Lord was recognised by their wicked deeds. Harshness has appeared, knowledge has diminished, and the Sunnah has been abandoned. Indeed, to Allāh we belong and to Him we shall return. (They are) confused, intoxicated, not Jews, nor Christians, nor Magians, that they might be excused.*
*Indeed, the believer did not take his religion from the people, but rather it came to him from Allāh, the Mighty and Majestic, so he took it. And indeed, the hypocrite gave the people his tongue but withheld his heart and his actions from Allāh.*
*So two new calamities have occurred in Islām: a man of evil opinion who claimed that Paradise is for whoever holds an opinion like his, so he drew his sword, shed the blood of the Muslims, and violated their sanctity; and a devoted one to luxury who worships the world; For its sake he becomes angry, and for it he fights, and for it he strives.*
*O, Subhan Allāh! What this Ummah has faced from a hypocrite who oppressed it and dominated it, and an apostate who abandoned the religion and rebelled against it! Two vile groups that have distressed every Muslim. O son of Ādam, your religion! Your religion! For it is your very flesh and your blood. If you are safe in it, what a comfort it is! And what a blessing it is! But if you are otherwise, then we seek refuge in Allāh. It is but a Fire that is never extinguished, a stone that never cools, and a soul that never dies.”*

[Al-Firyābī in Ṣifat al-Munāfiq (49); Isnād Ṣaḥīḥ]

الحسن، يقول: إنما الناس بين ثلاثة نفر: مؤمن ومنافق وكافر فأما المؤمن فعامل بطاعة الله عز وجل وأما الكافر فقد أذله الله تعالى كما رأيتم وأما المنافق فههنا وههنا في ‌الحجر ‌والبيوت ‌والطرق نعوذ بالله والله ما عرفوا ربهم بل عرفوا إنكارهم لربهم بأعمالهم الخبيثة ظهر الجفا وقل العلم وتركت السنة إنا لله وإنا إليه راجعون، حيارى سكارى ليسوا بيهود ولا نصارى ولا مجوس فيعذروا وقال: إن المؤمن لم يأخذ دينه عن الناس ولكن أتاه من قبل الله عز وجل فأخذه، وإن المنافق أعطى الناس لسانه ومنع الله قلبه وعمله. فحدثان أحدثا في الإسلام رجل ذو رأي سوء زعم أن الجنة لمن رأى مثل رأيه فسل سيفه وسفك دماء المسلمين واستحل حرمتهم، ومترف يعبد الدنيا لها يغضب وعليها يقاتل ولها يطلب وقال: يا سبحان الله ما لقيت هذه الأمة من منافق قهرها واستأثر عليها ومارق مرق من الدين فخرج عليها. صنفان خبيثان قد غما كل مسلم ، يا ابن آدم دينك دينك فإنما هو لحمك ودمك فإن تسلم بها فيالها من راحة ويا لها من نعمة وإن تكن الأخرى فنعوذ بالله فإنما هي نار لا تطفأ وحجر لا يبرد ونفس لا تموت

[الفريابي في صفة المنافق (٤٩) وسنده صحيح]

Utbah heard Umar bin Abdul `Aziz رحمه الله saying: 

لو قطعت يدي لرفعت ذراعي و لو قطعت ذراعي لرفعت ضبعي

 *"If my hands are cut off (for doing rafa yadain), then I would raise my arms; and if my arms are cut off then I would raise rest part of my arms (but I won't abandon doing rafa yadain)."* 

[Al-Khilafiyaat — vol. 2, pg: 355, No: 1691]

02/09/2025, 6:49 pm - Muzammil New: *Advices from al-Shāfi'ī when your friend does a mistake*
______________________________

Yūnus ibn ʿAbd al-Aʿlā said that l-Shāfiʿī said to me one day:
*O Yūnus, if you are informed of something you dislike about your friend, then beware of rushing to animosity and cutting the friendship bond, lest you become one of those who removed his certainty with a doubt. Rather, meet him and say to him: 'It has reached me about you such-and-such' and it is better that you name who informed you. If he denies it, then say to him: 'You are more truthful and more upright,' and do not add anything to that. And if he confesses to it and you see an excuse for it, then accept it from him. And if you do not see that, then say to him: 'What did you intend by what has reached me about you?' If he then mentions a matter as an excuse, accept it. And if he does not mention an excuse for it, and the path becomes constricted for you, then at that point establish it against him as a misdeed. Then, you have the choice: if you wish, you may repay him in equal without any addition, and if you wish, you may forgive him. And forgiveness is more conducive to Taqwá and more profound in nobility due to the saying of Allāh the Exalted: {And the recompense for an evil is an evil like thereof, but whoever pardons and makes reconciliation - his reward is from Allāh} [al-Shūrā: 40]. So, if your soul contests with you, urging for retaliation, then remember the good he did for you and do not diminish the remainder of his previous goodness because of this single misdeed for that is injustice in its very essence. And a righteous man used to say: 'May Allāh have mercy on one who repaid me for my wrongdoing without adding to it, nor diminishing a right that was due to me.' O Yūnus, if you have a friend, hold fast to him with both your hands, for indeed, making a friend is difficult and parting from him is easy. And a righteous man used to compare the ease of parting from a friend to a young boy who throws a great stone into a well; its throwing is easy for him, but its removal is difficult even for strong, sturdy men. So this is my counsel to you. And Salām.*

[Ḥilyat al-Awliyā (9/121); Isnād Ṣaḥīḥ]

يُونُسَ بْنَ عَبْدِ الْأَعْلَى، يَقُولُ: قَالَ لِي الشَّافِعِيُّ ذَاتَ يَوْمٍ: يَا يُونُسُ إِذَا بُلِّغْتَ عَنْ صَدِيقٍ لَكَ مَا تَكْرَهُهُ فَإِيَّاكَ أَنْ تُبَادِرَ بِالْعَدَاوَةِ وَقَطْعِ الْوَلَايَةِ فَتَكُونَ مِمَّنْ أَزَالَ يَقِينَهُ بِشَكٍ، وَلَكِنِ الْقَهُ، وَقُلْ لَهُ: بَلَغَنِي عَنْكَ كَذَا وَكَذَا وَأَجْدَرُ أَنْ تُسَمِّيَ الْمُبَلِّغَ فَإِنْ أَنْكَرَ ذَلِكَ فَقُلْ لَهُ: أَنْتَ أَصْدَقُ وَأَبَرُّ، وَلَا تَزِيدَنَّ عَلَى ذَلِكَ شَيْئًا. وَإِنِ اعْتَرَفَ بِذَلِكَ فَرَأَيْتَ لَهُ فِي ذَلِكَ وَجْهًا بِعُذْرٍ فَاقْبَلْ مِنْهُ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَرُدَّ ذَلِكَ فَقُلْ لَهُ: مَاذَا أَرَدْتَ بِمَا بَلَغَنِي عَنْكَ؟ فَإِنْ ذَكَرَ مَا لَهُ وَجْهٌ مِنَ الْعُذْرِ فَاقْبَلْهُ، وَإِنْ لَمْ يَذْكُرْ لِذَلِكَ وَجْهًا لِعُذْرٍ، وَضَاقَ عَلَيْكَ الْمَسْلَكُ فَحِينَئِذٍ أَثْبِتْهَا عَلَيْهِ سَيِّئَةً أَتَاهَا. ثُمَّ أَنْتَ فِي ذَلِكَ بِالْخِيَارِ إِنْ شِئْتَ كَافَأْتَهُ بِمِثْلِهِ مِنْ غَيْرِ زِيَادَةٍ وَإِنْ شِئْتَ عَفَوْتَ عَنْهُ، وَالْعَفْوُ أَبْلَغُ لِلتَّقْوَى، وَأَبْلَغُ فِي الْكَرْمِ؛ لِقَوْلِ اللَّهِ تَعَالَى: {وَجَزَاءُ سَيِّئَةٍ سَيِّئَةٍ مِثْلَهَا فَمَنْ عَفَا وَأَصْلِحَ فَأَجْرُهُ عَلَى اللَّهِ} [الشورى: ٤٠] فَإِنْ نَازَعَتْكَ نَفْسُكَ بِالْمُكَافَأَةِ فَاذْكُرْ فِيمَا سَبَقَ لَهُ لَدَيْكَ، وَلَا تَبْخَسْ بَاقِي إِحْسَانِهِ السَّالِفَ بِهَذِهِ السَّيِّئَةِ فَإِنَّ ذَلِكَ الظُّلْمُ بِعَيْنِهِ، وَقَدْ كَانَ الرَّجُلُ الصَّالِحُ يَقُولُ: رَحِمَ اللَّهُ مَنْ كَافَأَنِي عَلَى إِسَاءَتِي مِنْ غَيْرِ أَنْ يَزِيدَ وَلَا يَبْخَسَ حَقًّا لِي. يَا يونُسُ إِذَا كَانَ لَكَ صَدِيقٌ فَشُدَّ يَدَيْكَ بِهِ فَإِنَّ اتِّخَاذَ الصَّدِيقِ صَعْبٌ وَمُفَارَقَتُهُ سَهْلٌ. وَقَدْ كَانَ الرَّجُلُ الصَّالِحُ يُشَبِّهُ سُهُولَةَ مُفَارَقَةِ الصَّدِيقِ بِصَبِيٍّ يَطْرَحُ فِي الْبِئْرِ حَجَرًا عَظِيمًا فَيسْهُلُ طَرْحُهُ عَلَيْهِ، وَيَصْعُبُ إِخْرَاجُهُ عَلَى الرِّجَالِ البركِ فَهَذِهِ وَصِيَّتِي لَكَ. وَالسَّلَامُ

[حلية الأولياء (٩/١٢١) وسنده صحيح]

Some of the Salaf رحمه الله said:

I battled with my nafs for twenty years before it became upright. If you strive for long enough, and repent each time you sin, then your nafs will become upright.

But, this is something that doesn't happen over days or months; it requires long years.


[Hilayat al-Awliya', Abu Nuaym (rahimahullah), 7/5]

عن أبي طالب أنه سأل أبا عبد الله – أحمد بن حنبل - أقول : " معاوية خال المؤمنين " و " ابن عمر خال المؤمنين " ؟ قال : نعم ، معاوية أخو أم حبيبة بنت أبي سفيان زوج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ورحمهما ، وابن عمر أخو حفصة زوج النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم ورحمهما ، قلت : أقول معاوية خال المؤمنين ؟ قال : نعم .
" السنَّة " للخلال ( 2 / 433 ) طبعة دار الراية .
وعن هارون بن عبد الله أنه قال لأبي عبد الله – أحمد بن حنبل - : جاءني كتاب من " الرقة " أن قوماً قالوا : لا نقول معاوية خال المؤمنين ، فغضب ، وقال : ما اعتراضهم في هذا الموضع ؟ يُجْفَوْن حتى يتوبوا .
" السنَّة " للخلال ( 2 / 434 ) .
وعن محمد بن أبي هارون ومحمد بن أبي جعفر أن أبا الحارث حدثهم قال : وجهنا رقعة إلى أبي عبد الله – أحمد بن حنبل - ما تقول رحمك الله فيمن قال لا أقول إن معاوية كاتب الوحي ولا أقول إنه خال المؤمنين فإنه أخذها بالسيف غصباً ؟ قال أبو عبد الله : هذا قول سوء رديء ، يجانبون هؤلاء القوم ، ولا يجالسون ، ونبين أمرهم للناس .
" السنَّة " للخلال ( 2 / 434 ) .
وعن أبي بكر المروذي قال : قلت لأبي عبد الله – أحمد بن حنبل - أيما أفضل معاوية أو عمر بن عبد العزيز ؟ فقال : معاوية أفضل ، لسنا نقيس بأصحاب رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أحداً ، قال النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم " خير الناس قرني الذي بُعثت فيهم " .
" السنَّة " للخلال ( 2 / 434 ) .

03/09/2025, 8:49 pm - Mohamed Ahmed Abdulwahab: *Severity of arguments and not acting upon knowledge*
______________________________

al-Awzāʿī (may Allāh have mercy on him) said:
*"If Allāh wills evil for a people, He opens upon them argumentation and prevents them from action." (1)*

[Iqtiḍāʾ al-ʿIlm al-ʿAmal (122) and Tārīkh Dimashq (35/201); Isnād Ḥasan]

الأوزاعي، يقول: "إذا ‌أراد الله بقوم شرا فتح عليهم ‌الجدل ومنعهم ‌العمل"

[اقتضاء العلم العمل (١٢٢) وتاريخ دمشق (٣٥/٢٠١) وسنده حسن]

______________________________
*(1) The Prophet ﷺ said:*
*“Indeed, the most hated of men to Allah is the fiercely argumentative”* [al-Bukhārī (2457) & Muslim (2668)]

[Mohamed Ahmed Abdulwahab]

04/09/2025, 5:44 pm - +91 88229 56870: Imam ash-Shafi'ee - Poetry on how to respond to Fool:

"The fools speak to me with all vulgarity

So I hate to respond likewise in turn. they increase in their evil, so I increase in my patience"

Like an incense that becomes more fragrant when burned. So when the fool speaks do not respond, the strongest rebuttal is lack of acknowledgment.

If you address him he finds comfort, but if you ignore him he remains paralyzed

In another narration Imam ash-Shafi'i said: "If a fool speaks, do not answer him. The best answer to him is silence. If you answer him, it will only loosen his tongue. If you leave him, he will die of sadness."

Also ash-Shafi'i said: "A humiliation of knowledge is to argue with everyone who tries to argue with you, and to speak with everyone who tries to speak with you." "Manaqib ash-Shafi'i", 2/151,


Ye authentic h?

05/09/2025, 6:22 am - Mohamed Ahmed Abdulwahab: *{And this is My path, straight, so follow it; and do not follow (other) paths, for you will diverge from His path}* [6:153]
______________________________

ʿAbdullāh ibn Masʿūd (may Allāh be pleased with him) said:
*Allāh's Messenger ﷺ drew a line for us, then said: "This is Allah's path." Then he drew lines to its right and to its left, then he said: "These are paths." Yazīd (a narrator) said: "divergent paths." upon every one of these paths is a Shayṭān inviting to it." (1) Then he recited: {And this is My path, straight, so follow it; and do not follow (other) paths, for you will diverge from His path}.(2)*

[Aḥmad (4142), al-Ṭayālisī (241), Ibn Manṣūr (935), al-Dārimī (208), Ibn Waḍḍāḥ (75), Ibn Abī ʿĀṣim (17), al-Bazzār (1865), al-Sunnah by al-Marwazī (11), al-Nasāʾī in al-Kubrā (11109), Tafsīr Ibn Abī Ḥātim (8102), Musnad al-Shāshī (535-537), Ibn Ḥibbān (6), al-Sharīʿah (12), al-Targhīb wa al-Tarhīb by Qiwām al-Sunnah (351), al-Baghawī in his Tafsīr (3/205), and al-Anwār (1230); with Jayyid asānīd]

عبد الله بن مسعود، قال: خط لنا رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم خطا ثم قال: "هذا سبيل الله"، ثم خط خطوطا عن يمينه وعن شماله، ثم قال: "هذه سبل - قال يزيد: متفرقة - على كل سبيل منها شيطان يدعو إليه"، ثم قرأ: {وأن هذا صراطي مستقيما فاتبعوه ولا تتبعوا السبل فتفرق بكم عن سبيله}

[أحمد (٤١٤٢) والطيالسي (٢٤١) وابن منصور (٩٣٥) والدارمي (٢٠٨) وابن وضاح (٧٥) وابن أبي عاصم (١٧) والبزار (١٨٦٥) والسنة للمروزي (١١) والنسائي في الكبرى (١١١٠٩) وتفسير ابن أبي حاتم (٨١٠٢) ومسند الشاشي (٥٣٥-٥٣٧) وابن حبان (٦) والشريعة (١٢) والترغيب والترهيب لقوام السنة (٣٥١) والبغوي في التفسير (٣/٢٠٥) والأنوار (١٢٣٠) بأسانيد جياد]

Mujāhid said (regarding) *{and do not follow (other) paths}*:
*"the innovations and the doubtful matters."*

[Al-Dārimī (210), al-Sunnah by al-Marwazī (19 & 20), Ḥilyat al-Awliyāʾ (3/293), and al-Madkhal by al-Bayhaqī (1335); with Jayyid asānīd]

عن مجاهد {ولا تتبعوا ‌السبل} قال: ‌البدع والشبهات

[الدارمي (٢١٠) والسنة للمروزي (١٩ و٢٠) وحلية الأولياء (٣/٢٩٣) والمدخل للبيهقي (١٣٣٥) بأسانيد جياد]
______________________________
(1) This shows truth is one while falsehood has many paths.

(2) Ibn Hibban put this under the chapter: *"A mention of the report regarding what is obligatory upon a person: to adhere to the Sunan of al-Muṣṭafā ﷺ, and to protect himself from everyone who rejects them from the People of Innovation, even if they make that beautiful in his eyes and adorn it for him."*
05/09/2025, 6:40 am - +92 316 4986376: There's a version in Musnad Ahmad 16970 (It's Daif/Weak but Will double check the auth)

For now, something similar but (Sahih - Sunan Ad Darimi : 98) from the sayings of Hassan ibn Atiyyah (A Tabiee)

No people introduce an innovation in their religion except that Allah removes an equivalent amount from their sunnah, then not restoring it to them till the day of resurrection.

قال الدارمي: أَخْبَرَنَا أَبُو الْمُغِيرَةِ ، حَدَّثَنَا الْأَوْزَاعِيُّ ، عَنْ حَسَّان قَالَ: «مَا ابْتَدَعَ قَوْمٌ بِدْعَةً فِي دِينِهِمْ إِلَّا نَزَعَ اللَّهُ مِنْ سُنَّتِهِمْ مِثْلَهَا ثُمَّ لَا يُعِيدُهَا إِلَيْهِمْ إِلَى يَوْمِ الْقِيَامَة.» <This message was edited>
